}






function
google_ad_request_done(google_ads)
{




window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Bloc_Party';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"bloc,_,party,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Bloc
Party</b>
are
a
British
<a
href="/wiki/Indie_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Indie
rock">indie
rock</a>
band,
composed
of
<a
href="/wiki/Kele_Okereke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kele
Okereke">Kele
Okereke</a>
(lead
vocals,
rhythm
guitar),
<a
href="/wiki/Russell_Lissack?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Russell
Lissack">Russell
Lissack</a>
(lead
guitar),
<a
href="/wiki/Gordon_Moakes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gordon
Moakes">Gordon
Moakes</a>
(bass
guitar,
<a
href="/wiki/Synthesizer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Synthesizer">synths</a>,
backing
vocals,
<a
href="/wiki/Glockenspiel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glockenspiel">glockenspiel</a>),
and
Matt
Tong
(drums,
backing
vocals).
Their
brand
of
music
is
said
to
have
been
drawn
from
such
bands
as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Cure?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Cure">The
Cure</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_2-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Mogwai?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mogwai">Mogwai</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_2-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Siouxsie_and_the_Banshees?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Siouxsie
and
the
Banshees">Siouxsie
and
the
Banshees</a><sup
id="cite_ref-brunswick_3-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-brunswick-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
in
their
more
recent
work,
<a
href="/wiki/Radiohead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-gigwise_4-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gigwise-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
was
formed
at
the
1999
<a
href="/wiki/Reading_and_Leeds_Festivals?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading
and
Leeds
Festivals">Reading
Festival</a>
by
Okereke
and
Lissack.
They
went
through
a
variety
of
names
before
settling
on
Bloc
Party
in
2003.
Moakes
joined
the
band
after
answering
an
advert
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/NME?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME">NME</a></i>
magazine,
while
Tong
was
picked
via
an
audition.
Bloc
Party
got
their
break
by
giving
<a
href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BBC
Radio
1">BBC
Radio
1</a>
DJ
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Lamacq?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Lamacq">Steve
Lamacq</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Franz_Ferdinand_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Franz
Ferdinand
(band)">Franz
Ferdinand</a>'s
lead
singer,
<a
href="/wiki/Alex_Kapranos?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alex
Kapranos">Alex
Kapranos</a>,
a
copy
of
their
demo
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/She%27s_Hearing_Voices?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="She's
Hearing
Voices">She's
Hearing
Voices</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>In
February
2005,
the
band
released
their
debut
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Silent_Alarm?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Silent
Alarm">Silent
Alarm</a></i>.
It
was
critically
acclaimed
and
was
named
Indie
Album
of
the
Year
at
the
2006
<a
href="/wiki/PLUG_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="PLUG
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">PLUG
Awards</a>
and
<i>NME</i>
Album
of
the
year
which
both
honour
<a
href="/wiki/Indie_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Indie
music"
class="mw-redirect">indie
music</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-PLUG6_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-PLUG6-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
That
year,
the
record
was
also
certified
<a
href="/wiki/Platinum_record?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Platinum
record"
class="mw-redirect">platinum</a>
in
Britain.
The
band
built
on
this
success
in
2007
with
the
release
of
their
second
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/A_Weekend_in_the_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Weekend
in
the
City">A
Weekend
in
the
City</a></i>,
which
reached
a
peak
of
number
two
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Albums
Chart">UK
Albums
Chart</a>
and
number
twelve
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>.
In
August
2008,
Bloc
Party
released
their
third
studio
record,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Intimacy_(Bloc_Party_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Intimacy
(Bloc
Party
album)">Intimacy</a></i>
which
entered
the
UK
Albums
Chart
at
number
eight
and
number
eighteen
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
200.
The
band
went
on
a
hiatus
in
October
2009
to
focus
on
<a
href="/wiki/Side_project?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Side
project">side
projects</a>.
They
reunited
in
September
2011,
and
shortly
thereafter
released
their
fourth
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Four_(Bloc_Party_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Four
(Bloc
Party
album)">Four</a></i>,
which
entered
the
UK
Albums
Chart
at
number
three.
In
2013,
Bloc
Party
released
their
third
EP
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Nextwave_Sessions?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Nextwave
Sessions">The
Nextwave
Sessions</a></i>
in
August;
the
band
then
began
an
indefinite
hiatus
to
continue
with
their
respective
side
projects.
As
of
May
2012<sup
class="plainlinks
noprint
asof-tag
update"
style="display:none;"><a
rel="nofollow"
class="external
text"
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?title=Bloc_Party&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,
Bloc
Party
have
sold
two
million
albums
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
style="overflow:hidden;height:;">








&nbsp;







</div>







<table
id="tblToc"
border="0"
cellpadding="0"

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bloc_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Formation_and_rising_popularity_.281999.E2.80.932004.29">Formation
and
rising
popularity
(1999â€“2004)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bloc_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Formation
and
rising
popularity
(1999â€“2004)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Russell_Lissack?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Russell
Lissack">Russell
Lissack</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Kele_Okereke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kele
Okereke">Kele
Okereke</a>
first
met
in
1998
in
London.
Lissack
had
attended
<a
href="/wiki/Bancroft%27s_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bancroft's
School">Bancroft's
School</a>,
while
Okereke
attended
<a
href="/wiki/Ilford_County_High_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ilford
County
High
School">Ilford
County
High
School</a>,
then
<a
href="/wiki/Trinity_Catholic_High_School,_Woodford_Green?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trinity
Catholic
High
School,
Woodford
Green">Trinity
Catholic
High
School,
Woodford
Green</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Sixth_form?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sixth
form">sixth
form</a>.
They
bumped
into
each
other
again
in
1999
at
Reading
Festival
and
decided
to
form
a
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-Guardian_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Guardian-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Gordon_Moakes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gordon
Moakes">Gordon
Moakes</a>
joined
after
answering
an
advert
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/NME?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME">NME</a></i>,
and
drummer
Matt
Tong
joined
after
an
audition.<sup
id="cite_ref-Guardian_7-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Guardian-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
going
through
a
variety
of
names,
such
as
Union,
The
Angel
Range,
and
Diet,
the
band
settled
on
Bloc
Party
in
September
2003,
a
play
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Block_party?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Block
party">block
party</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
has
said
that
the
name
was
not
intended
to
be
an
allusion
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eastern
Bloc">Soviet
Bloc</a>
or
the
Canadian
political
party
<a
href="/wiki/Bloc_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bloc
Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois">Bloc
Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois</a>.
However,
Moakes
said
on
the
group's
official
Internet
forum
that
it
was
more
a
merging
of
the
eastern
&quot;Blocs&quot;
and
the
western
&quot;parties&quot;,
in
the
political
sense.
He
also
notes
that
the
name
was
not
explicitly
driven
by
politics,
but
rather
it
&quot;looked,
sounded,
seemed
fine
so
we
went
with
it.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<table
class="mbox-small"
style="border:1px
solid
#aaa;
background-color:#f9f9f9;">

/>












</div>

</td>











<td

<div

&quot;Banquet&quot;
was
Bloc
Party's
first
and
only
release
by














<a
href="/wiki/Moshi_Moshi_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Moshi
Moshi
Records">Moshi
Moshi</a>,
and
is
typical
of
their
early














<a
href="/wiki/Indie_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Indie
rock">indie
rock</a>
style.












</div>

/></td>










</tr>










<tr>











<td
colspan="2"
class="mbox-text"
style="line-height:1.1em;"><span

playing

file?

<a

title="Wikipedia:Media

help</a>.</i></span></td>

</table>








<p>In
November
2003,
Bloc
Party
had
their
track
&quot;The
Marshals
Are
Dead&quot;
featured
on
a
compilation
CD
called
<i>The
New
Cross</i>
released
by
<a
href="/wiki/Angular_Recording_Corporation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Angular
Recording
Corporation">Angular
Recording
Corporation</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
then
released
their
debut
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/She%27s_Hearing_Voices?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="She's
Hearing
Voices">She's
Hearing
Voices</a>&quot;
on
the
then
fledgling
record
label
<a
href="/wiki/Trash_Aesthetics?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trash
Aesthetics">Trash
Aesthetics</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
got
their
break
after
Okereke
went
to
a
<a
href="/wiki/Franz_Ferdinand_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Franz
Ferdinand
(band)">Franz
Ferdinand</a>
concert
in
2003,
and
gave
a
copy
of
&quot;She's
Hearing
Voices&quot;
to
both
lead
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Alex_Kapranos?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alex
Kapranos">Alex
Kapranos</a>
and
BBC
Radio
1
DJ
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Lamacq?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Lamacq">Steve
Lamacq</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lamacq
subsequently
played
the
song
on
his
radio
show,
labelling
the
track
&quot;genius&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
invited
them
to
record
a
live
session
for
the
show.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
buzz
generated
off
the
back
of
the
single
led
to
another
release,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Banquet/Staying_Fat?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Banquet/Staying
Fat">Banquet/Staying
Fat</a>&quot;,
this
time
through
<a
href="/wiki/Moshi_Moshi_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Moshi
Moshi
Records">Moshi
Moshi
Records</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
to
the
eventual
signing
with
independent
label
<a
href="/wiki/Wichita_Recordings?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wichita
Recordings">Wichita
Recordings</a>
in
April
2004.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Silent_Alarm_.282004.E2.80.932006.29"><i>Silent
Alarm</i>
(2004â€“2006)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bloc_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Silent
Alarm
(2004â€“2006)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kele_Russell.JPG"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Kele_Russell.JPG/220px-Kele_Russell.JPG"
width="220"
height="235"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Kele_Russell.JPG/330px-Kele_Russell.JPG
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/3/31/Kele_Russell.JPG
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kele_Russell.JPG"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Bloc
Party's
Lissack
and
Okereke
on
stage
in











<a
href="/wiki/Cardiff?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>
in
October
2005









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Bloc
Party's
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Silent_Alarm?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Silent
Alarm">Silent
Alarm</a></i>,
was
released
in
February
2005
and
was
met
with
universal
<a
href="/wiki/Music_critic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
critic"
class="mw-redirect">critical</a>
acclaim.<sup
id="cite_ref-Metacritic_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Metacritic-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
voted
'Album
of
the
Year'
for
2005
by
<i>NME</i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
reached
number
3
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Albums
Chart">UK
Albums
Chart</a>
before
being
certified
<a
href="/wiki/Platinum_record?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Platinum
record"
class="mw-redirect">platinum</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-everyhit_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-everyhit-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-SAplat_20-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SAplat-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
single
from
the
album,
&quot;So
Here
We
Are/Positive
Tension&quot;,
made
the
top
5
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Top_40?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Top
40"
class="mw-redirect">UK
Top
40</a>
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-everyhit_19-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-everyhit-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
Further
singles
&quot;Banquet&quot;
(which
reached
number
13
in
<i>NME'</i>s
'Top
50
Singles
of
2005'),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Helicopter_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Helicopter
(song)">Helicopter</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pioneers_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pioneers
(song)">Pioneers</a>&quot;,
whilst
failing
to
repeat
this
success,
still
managed
to
reach
the
UK
top
20.<sup
id="cite_ref-everyhit_19-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-everyhit-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
animated
video
for
&quot;Pioneers&quot;,
made
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Shoreditch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shoreditch">Shoreditch</a>-based
Minivegas
design
agency,<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
was
top
of
the
<i>NME</i>
video
charts
for
4
weeks.
<i>NME</i>
tagged
them
as
&quot;art-rock&quot;
at
that
time
but
the
band
felt
it
was
too
limited.<sup
id="cite_ref-Interview_2004_22-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Interview_2004-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
received
positive
reviews
from
critics
in
the
United
States
and
they
toured
there
heavily
in
the
18
months
that
followed
the
release
of
<i>Silent
Alarm</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-live06_23-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-live06-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
early
2006,
they
finished
their
tour
with
sold
out
shows
in
Los
Angeles,
Miami
and
<a
href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Berkeley,
California">Berkeley</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-live06_23-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-live06-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
went
on
to
sell
more
than
350,000
copies
in
North
America
and
over
a
million
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-SAplat_20-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SAplat-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
this
success,
the
established
electronic
group,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Chemical_Brothers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Chemical
Brothers">The
Chemical
Brothers</a>,
soon
collaborated
with
Okereke
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Believe_(The_Chemical_Brothers_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Believe
(The
Chemical
Brothers
song)">Believe</a>&quot;,
a
track
on
their
<i><a
href="/wiki/Push_the_Button_(The_Chemical_Brothers_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Push
the
Button
(The
Chemical
Brothers
album)">Push
the
Button</a></i>
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="A_Weekend_in_the_City_.282006.E2.80.932008.29"><i>A
Weekend
in
the
City</i>
(2006â€“2008)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bloc_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
A
Weekend
in
the
City
(2006â€“2008)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Bloc
Party's
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/A_Weekend_in_the_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Weekend
in
the
City">A
Weekend
in
the
City</a></i>,
was
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Jacknife_Lee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jacknife
Lee">Garret
&quot;Jacknife&quot;
Lee</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
released
in
February
2007,<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
although
it
was
<a
href="/wiki/Internet_leak?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Internet
leak">leaked</a>
in
November
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-EW_33-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-EW-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
became
available
for
download
on
the
UK
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes_Store?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes
Store">iTunes
Store</a>
before
the
physical
release,
and
reached
the
number
2
spot
on
the
UK
Albums
Chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
also
reached
number
2
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ARIA
Charts">Australian</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ultratop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

charts,<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
debuted
at
number
12
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>,
with
48,000
copies
sold.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Prayer_(Bloc_Party_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Prayer
(Bloc
Party
song)">The
Prayer</a>&quot;,
was
released
on
29
January,<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
became
the
band's
highest
charting
single
in
the
British
Top
40,
reaching
number
4.<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
build
up
to
the
release
of
the
album,
BBC
Radio
1
DJ
<a
href="/wiki/Zane_Lowe?qsrc=3044"

title="Zane
Lowe">Zane
Lowe</a>
aired
a
live
set
by
the
band
from
<a
href="/wiki/Maida_Vale?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Maida
Vale">Maida
Vale</a>
studios
on
30
January
2007,
featuring
a
mix
of
old
and
new
songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
1
February
2007,
<i>A
Weekend
in
the
City</i>
was
made
available
to
listen
to
for
free
through
the
Bloc
Party's
official
MySpace
page.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Intimacy_.282008.E2.80.932009.29"><i>Intimacy</i>
(2008â€“2009)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bloc_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"

(2008â€“2009)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Mercury_(song)?qsrc=3044"

title="Mercury
(song)">Mercury</a>&quot;
was

third
album
in

2008.<sup
id="cite_ref-ZL08_57-0"
class="reference"><a

Again
produced
by
Jacknife
Lee
and
Paul
Epworth,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Intimacy_(Bloc_Party_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Intimacy
(Bloc
Party
album)">Intimacy</a></i>
was
rush-released
later
that
month,
with
the
album
available
to
download
3
days
after
an
announcement
in
August
2008.
Later
in
the
month
the
band
played
second
on
the
bill
at

and

Festivals<sup
id="cite_ref-BBC_Bloc_Party_58-0"

before

the
<a

Festival">Hydro

in
<a
href="/wiki/Argyll?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Argyll">Argyll</a>,
Scotland.<sup
id="cite_ref-Connect_review_59-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Connect_review-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During

of
2008,
the
band
went
on
a
short

of

which

<a

in
<a

as
well
as
the
band's
first
ever
American
college
show
at
<a

University">Syracuse
University</a>.<sup

date
of
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV2">MTV2</a>'s
and
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

&quot;Gonzo
on
Tour&quot;
on
19
October
2008.<sup

A

&quot;<a

(song)">Talons</a>&quot;
was

CD

and
was

An
album
of

<i>Intimacy</i>,
<i><a

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="One_More_Chance_and_hiatus_.282009.E2.80.932011.29"><i>One
More
Chance</i>
and
hiatus
(2009â€“2011)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bloc_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
One
More
Chance
and
hiatus
(2009â€“2011)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
July
2009,
Okereke
stated
that
the
band
did
not
have
a
current
recording
contract
and
had
no
obligation
or
pressure
to
release
a
new
album
in
the
foreseeable
future;
he
went
on
to
suggest
that
the
release
of
a
fourth
album
was
on
an
indefinite
timescale.<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
new
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/One_More_Chance_(Bloc_Party_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
More
Chance
(Bloc
Party
song)">One
More
Chance</a>&quot;,
was
released
in
August
2009.
The
song
did
not
appear
on
<i>Intimacy</i>
and
was
produced
by
Jacknife
Lee.
After
this
the
group
went
on
a
hiatus,
with
the
members
unsure
as
to
whether
they
would
carry
on.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
this
period
of
hiatus
Lissack
revived
his
project
<a
href="/wiki/Pin_Me_Down?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pin
Me
Down">Pin
Me
Down</a><sup
id="cite_ref-nme_pinmedown_69-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nme_pinmedown-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
joined
the
live
line-up
of
Irish
rock-band
<a
href="/wiki/Ash_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ash
(band)">Ash</a>
as
guitarist
and
synthesiser
player
on
their
touring
for
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/A%E2%80%93Z_Series?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aâ€“Z
Series">Aâ€“Z
Series</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup>
Moakes
formed
the
group
<a
href="/wiki/Young_Legionnaire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Young
Legionnaire">Young
Legionnaire</a>
with
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_Mullen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul
Mullen">Paul
Mullen</a>,
vocalist
&amp;
guitarist
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Automatic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Automatic">The
Automatic</a>,
and
William
Bowerman,
drummer
for
<a
href="/wiki/La_Roux?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="La
Roux">La
Roux</a>,
releasing
a
single,
&quot;Colossus&quot;
in
August
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup>
Okereke
released
a
solo
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Boxer_(Kele_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Boxer
(Kele
album)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Boxer</a></i>,
in
June
2010.
Produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Hudson_Mohawke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hudson
Mohawke">Hudson
Mohawke</a>
and
XXXChange,
its
release
was
preceded
by
the
single
&quot;Tenderoni&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-74"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
Rumours
throughout
2011
suggested
Okereke
had
left
the
group
to
focus
on
solo
work,
though
these
were
denied
by
other
band
members.<sup
id="cite_ref-75"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Frenchkiss_76-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Frenchkiss-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Bloc
Party
started
writing
material
for
a
fourth
album
in
2011,<sup
id="cite_ref-77"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-guardian6-4-11_78-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-guardian6-4-11-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
but
decided
not
to
play
live.<sup
id="cite_ref-guardian6-4-11_78-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-guardian6-4-11-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
meantime
Okereke
finished
an
EP
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Hunter_(Kele_EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Hunter
(Kele
EP)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Hunter</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-KeleTheHunterNME_79-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KeleTheHunterNME-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
stated
they
intend
to
release
a
new
album
in
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
May
2012,
Bloc
Party
announced
<i><a
href="/wiki/Four_(Bloc_Party_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Four
(Bloc
Party
album)">Four</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-81"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-83"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
was
released
on
20
August
2012,
after
being
made
available
to
stream
in
its
entirety
for
over
a
week
preceding
release.
The
album
was
recorded
with
Alex
Newport,
who
had
previously
worked
with
<a
href="/wiki/At_The_Drive_In?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="At
The
Drive
In"
class="mw-redirect">At
The
Drive
In</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Mars_Volta?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Mars
Volta">The
Mars
Volta</a>,
in
New
York
City.
Bloc
Party
released
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Octopus_(Bloc_Party_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Octopus
(Bloc
Party
song)">Octopus</a>&quot;
that
July
and
later
released
another
single
entitled
&quot;Day
Four&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-84"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
released
&quot;Kettling&quot;
on
12
November
2012,
followed
by
&quot;Truth&quot;
on
25
February
2013.
<i>Four</i>
peaked
at
numer
three
on
the
UK
Albums
Chart
and
at
number
36
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
200.<sup
id="cite_ref-85"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

during

[...]
the

&quot;French
Exit&quot;

Some

to

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_style">Musical
style</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bloc_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
style">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Bloc
Party's
brand
of
guitar
rock
draws
on
influences
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Cure?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Cure">The
Cure</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Joy_Division?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joy
Division">Joy
Division</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Sonic_Youth?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sonic
Youth">Sonic
Youth</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_2-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Blur_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blur
(band)">Blur</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-91"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Smiths?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Smiths">The
Smiths</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Guardian_7-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Guardian-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
Okereke
has
also
stated
that
Mogwai's
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mogwai_Young_Team?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mogwai
Young
Team">Mogwai
Young
Team</a></i>
changed
his
life
by
being
his
musical
&quot;year
zero&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-92"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup>
Okereke
also
cites
<a
href="/wiki/Suede_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Suede
(band)">Suede</a>
as
a
major
influence,
he
says
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dog_Man_Star?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dog
Man
Star">Dog
Man
Star</a></i>
was
the
first
record
he
fell
in
love
with.<sup
id="cite_ref-93"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>
Particular
parallels
were
made
between
Bloc
Party
and
<a
href="/wiki/Gang_of_Four_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gang
of
Four
(band)">Gang
of
Four</a>
upon
their
arrival
on
the
music
scene,<sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_2-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
yet
the
band
were
&quot;mildly
infuriated&quot;
at
such
references,
claiming
they
had
never
&quot;particularly
liked&quot;
Gang
of
Four.<sup
id="cite_ref-EW_33-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-EW-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
To
achieve
their
unique
style,
numerous
delay
and
other
<a
href="/wiki/Effects_pedals?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Effects
pedals"
class="mw-redirect">effects
pedals</a>
are
implemented.<sup
id="cite_ref-94"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
recording
of
second
album
<i>A
Weekend
in
the
City</i>,
the
band
suggested
it
would
contain
&quot;some
truly
<a
href="/wiki/R%27n%27B?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="R'n'B"
class="mw-redirect">R'n'B</a>
styled
beats,
a
song
where
[Tong]
and
[Moakes]
play
drums
simultaneously
[with]
both
eggshell-thin
fragility
and
trouser-flapping
hugeness&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-95"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup>
as
opposed
to
their
typical
sound.
The
style
has
been
compared
to
and
inspired
by
such
bands
as
<a
href="/wiki/Radiohead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Depeche_Mode?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Depeche
Mode">Depeche
Mode</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bj&ouml;rk">Bj&ouml;rk</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-gigwise_4-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gigwise-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Some
of
the
most
noticeable
changes
between
debut
<i>Silent
Alarm</i>
and
<i>A
Weekend
in
the
City</i>
are
that
the
songs
became
more
layered
and
less
raw
due
to
inclusion
of
<a
href="/wiki/String_arrangement?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="String
arrangement"
class="mw-redirect">string
arrangements</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-AWITC_96-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AWITC-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>With
the
release
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Flux_(Bloc_Party_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Flux
(Bloc
Party
song)"
class="mw-redirect">Flux</a>&quot;,
Bloc
Party's
style
became
even
more
diverse
with
the
inclusion
of
electronic
music.<sup
id="cite_ref-AWITC_96-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AWITC-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Mercury_(Bloc_Party_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mercury
(Bloc
Party
song)"
class="mw-redirect">Mercury</a>&quot;
saw
Bloc
Party
distance
themselves
even
further
from
the
traditional
guitar
band
set-up
by
experimenting
with
dark
electronic
sounds
and
a
<a
href="/wiki/Brass_section?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brass
section">brass
section</a>
inspired
by
<a
href="/wiki/Siouxsie_and_the_Banshees?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Siouxsie
and
the
Banshees">Siouxsie
and
the
Banshees</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-brunswick_3-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-brunswick-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-elecBillboard_97-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-elecBillboard-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
third
album
<i>Intimacy</i>
also
features
synths,
processed
drum
beats
and
<a
href="/wiki/Drum_loops?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drum
loops"
class="mw-redirect">loops</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Vocoder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vocoder">vocal
manipulation</a>,
and
choral
arrangements.<sup
id="cite_ref-intimacy_98-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-intimacy-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup>
Even
though
the
album
is
influenced
by
electronic
music,
the
band
still
has
not
lost
their
feel
for
guitar
music.
For
example,
in
a
recent
interview,
Okereke
said
that
the
band
is
starting
to
miss
their
more
traditional
sound,
and
confirmed
that
may
be
the
way
fourth
album
is
headed.<sup
id="cite_ref-99"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
Tong
contradicted
this,
stating:
&quot;There's
every
chance
we
might
go
back
to
more
orthodox
arrangements
or
things
that
resemble
a
traditional
band
but
I
don't
think
we'll
ever
write
songs
like
we
did
on
<i>Silent
Alarm</i>
again.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-100"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
2009
<a
href="/wiki/Vice_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vice
Records"
class="mw-redirect">Vice
Records</a>
mix
lists
the
following
songs
Bloc
Party
are
influenced
by:
Eagle
Boston's
&quot;Wild
Wild
Ost&quot;,
<a
href="/wiki/Pylon_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pylon
(band)">Pylon</a>'s
&quot;Working
Is
No
Problem&quot;,
<a
href="/wiki/Delta_5?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Delta
5">Delta
5</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Singles_%26_Sessions_1979%E2%80%931981?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Singles
&amp;
Sessions
1979â€“1981">Mind
Your
Own
Business</a>&quot;,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Foxx?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Foxx">John
Foxx</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Metamatic?qsrc=3044#Track_listing"
title="Metamatic">Underpass</a>&quot;,
<a
href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Prince
(musician)">Prince</a>'s
&quot;<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

(also
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cover
song"
class="mw-redirect">covered</a>
live),
Sonic

&quot;<a

Jr.">Dinosaur

<p>Bloc
Party
have
had
several
nominations
from
a
number
of
different
awarding
bodies
during
their
recording
career.
The
band
themselves
were
nominated
for
'Best
New
Artist'
at
the
2005
<a
href="/wiki/NME_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME
Awards"><i>NME</i>
Awards</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-102"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
were
also
up
for
the
'Best
Alternative
Act'
category
at
the
2005
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Europe
Music
Awards">MTV
Europe
Music
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-103"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2006,
Bloc
Party
were
nominated
for
another
<i>NME</i>
Award,
this
time
in
the
'Best
British
Band'
category.<sup
id="cite_ref-NME6_104-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NME6-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
were
also
shortlisted
for
three
<a
href="/wiki/PLUG_Independent_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="PLUG
Independent
Music
Awards">PLUG
Awards</a>:
'New
Artist
of
the
Year'
in
2005,<sup
id="cite_ref-PLUG5_105-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-PLUG5-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
'Artist
of
the
Year'
and
'Live
Act
of
the
Year'
in
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-PLUG6_5-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-PLUG6-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/19th_GLAAD_Media_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="19th
GLAAD
Media
Awards">19th
GLAAD
Media
Awards</a>
in
2008,
they
were
nominated
in
the
'Music
Artist'
category
for
their
work
on
second
album
<i>A
Weekend
in
the
City</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-106"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Their
debut
album
<i>Silent
Alarm</i>
was
nominated
for
the
2005
<a
href="/wiki/Mercury_Music_Prize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mercury
Music
Prize"
class="mw-redirect">Mercury
Music
Prize</a>
and
won
the
NME
award
for
'Best
Album'.<sup
id="cite_ref-107"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
also
nominated
as
'Album
of
the
Year'
at
three
different
ceremonies:
the
<a
href="/wiki/New_Pantheon_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Pantheon
Music
Award"
class="mw-redirect">New
Pantheon
Music
Award</a>
(<a
href="/wiki/Shortlist_Music_Prize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shortlist
Music
Prize">Shortlist
Music
Prize</a>),<sup
id="cite_ref-108"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
2006
<i>NME</i>
Awards,<sup
id="cite_ref-NME6_104-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NME6-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
2006
PLUG
Awards,
where
&quot;Helicopter&quot;
was
also
up
for
'Best
Music
Video'.<sup
id="cite_ref-PLUG6_5-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-PLUG6-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
record
won
the
award
for
'Best
Indie
Rock
Album'
at
the
2006
PLUG
Awards.<sup
id="cite_ref-PLUG6_5-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-PLUG6-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
2008
<i>NME</i>
Awards,
&quot;Flux&quot;
was
nominated
in
three
different
categories:
'Best
Track',
'Best
Video'
and
'Best
Dancefloor
Filler'.<sup
id="cite_ref-109"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>




</div>
